## Task 2B runtime authority-tree hardening checkpoint — 2026-07-15

The independent review found three contract risks and the implementation now
addresses them in a bounded, fail-closed slice. Core static-authority graph
validation now preserves the documented distinction between raw artifact
receipt hashes and semantic static-generation ledger/bundle hashes; the
rebuild loader remains the byte-backed raw-hash verifier. A focused regression
proves that a raw receipt may differ from the semantic slot without weakening
the role/path contract (**8/8 Core tests**, **26/26 rebuild/loader tests**).

The runtime context now reads and verifies every artifact declared by the
selected input, static, and overlap generation trees, rejects orphan or
missing files, binds the overlap current pointer to the static-selected
generation, and joins overlap universe/policy/normalizer hashes back to the
rich bundle. The input generation is hash-selected from the static generation;
its self-hash, raw artifact bytes, evidence bundle hash, record-stream bytes,
and exact source-generation set are checked. The context proof now includes
input-generation bytes and an aggregate source-authority proof. File reads use
contained canonical paths, `O_NOFOLLOW`, and a post-read path-consistency
check.

The fixture is fully materialized for this boundary: it publishes actual
tool-authority intent/receipt objects, source-generation authorities, input
generation/artifacts, overlap generation/current/envelopes, and raw static
artifact receipts. Focused context/disposition coverage remains **2 files / 15
tests** (13 + 2), and now includes input/overlap missing-orphan artifacts and
stale overlap-current rejection. Recursive gates are green: Core **226/226**,
website **38/38**, engine **59/59**, and SlopBrick **3,620 passed / 9 skipped**
across **316 passed / 5 skipped test files**. Recursive typecheck/build and
`git diff --check` pass.

This runtime boundary is intentionally quarantine-only. Any
`independent_review` source generation fails closed until the mutating adapter
loads and verifies its persisted `source-semantic-authority.json`; source
review shape alone cannot promote a candidate. The legacy prebuilt publisher
is still metadata-tolerant and no mutating rebuild/recovery CLI exists. No
corpus labels/bytes, repository pulls, manifests, package versions, remotes,
releases, publishes, or deployments changed. Census/readiness remains
**329/329** reviewed sources, **452,382** quarantined/unrepresented units,
zero candidate/eligible units, with blockers `static_authority_unavailable`
and `witness_authority_unavailable`.

Remaining ordered work: independent release review; implement the mutating
rebuild/recovery adapter with a coherent cross-object snapshot and candidate
semantic-authority loading; then replay the real corpus context. Do not
promote labels or pull more repositories while the authority blockers remain.

## Task 2B candidate-aware mutating authority-rebuild adapter checkpoint — 2026-07-15

The bounded adapter is implemented in
`packages/slopbrick/src/calibration/v103/admission-authority-rebuild-adapter.ts`
and recorded in
`.superpowers/sdd/task-2b-runtime-adapter-report.md`. It composes the existing
transactional publisher/recovery path, strict byte-backed graph loader, and
indexed tool-authority resolver. Before the first filesystem mutation it
requires the fixed `admission-static-ledgers-v1` /
`authority:overlap` receipt chain and compares its derived snapshot with the
static-generation snapshot. Hash-only caller metadata cannot satisfy this
preflight. Runtime selector shape/values, graph self-hashes/byte pairs, and
replace prior-current evidence are also validated before the publisher can
create a lock; custom read paths are limited to contained admission-root prior
evidence.

At the publisher's durable `complete` boundary, before journal cleanup, the
adapter reopens the exact proposal, input-generation, static-generation,
current, source-generation, artifact, source-proposal, independent-review
approval, and candidate semantic-authority bytes. It compares every reopened
object and raw byte to the publication graph, returns one raw-byte graph proof,
and performs a second reopen after successful publication. Complete-boundary
verification failures remain pending/recoverable; post-return failures carry
the publication result and diagnostics. Recovery uses the same preflight and
reopen path; recovery of a journal already at the `complete` phase invokes
that strict hook before journal cleanup.

Focused coverage is **5 files / 53 tests** (adapter 7, publication/recovery
15, loader 10, graph 16, overlap join 5). SlopBrick typecheck and build pass;
the package-wide one-worker gate passes **317 files / 5 skipped; 3,627 tests /
9 skipped** under a 2 GiB heap cap. Existing Zod declaration warnings and
expected worker-fixture stderr remain non-fatal. No corpus, manifest, label,
repository acquisition, package version, remote ref, release, publish, or
deployment state changed. The census remains **329/329** reviewed sources,
**452,382** quarantined/unrepresented units, zero candidate/eligible units,
and blockers `static_authority_unavailable` and
`witness_authority_unavailable`.

The explicit package-local self-scan is diagnostic rather than a release gate
in this branch: it analyzed 235 files without parse/timeout/crash/internal
failures, but reported AI Slop Score **17.3** against the configured 15
threshold (157 active low/medium diagnostics, 100/100 security, zero security
findings). The prior baseline was rejected for a config-hash mismatch, so no
new baseline was accepted. The score is recorded for follow-up refactoring or
calibration-policy review; it must not be described as a passing release
self-scan.

This is a library boundary, not the mutating CLI or real-corpus admission. The
runtime context remains responsible for opening and joining the complete
overlap generation/envelope tree. Reopens are sequential and fail closed, but
there is no cross-object atomic snapshot under concurrent writers yet. The
existing publisher still materializes proposal and input-generation finals
directly before later transaction-owned promotions; fully staging those paths
is a separate hardening slice. Next: independent review of this adapter,
then add the CLI only if that review passes, and only afterward replay the
real static/witness context against the corpus. Do not pull repositories or
promote labels while the authority blockers remain.

## Task 2B current control-plane and self-scan audit — 2026-07-15

The post-adapter audit did not find a safe path to real v10.3 admission yet.
The centralized corpus at `/Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3` contains
approximately 3.8 GiB across `sources`, `review`, and `quarantine`; the
`sources` tree alone contains **11,127** regular non-`.git` source-tree files.
The repository inventory has
**317** pinned checkout records (**225** declared AI and **92** declared human);
all local paths exist and all recorded Git heads match their pinned commit
SHA, but these are declared polarities, not verified labels. Seventeen
checkouts have no root license record. The genesis register and review files
contain **329/329** entries, while the streamed inventories contain **224,903**
declared-AI and **227,479** declared-human units; no unit has a verified
admission label.

The correct genesis replay (`genesis-register-v1.json` plus
`genesis-source-reviews-v1.json`) remains fail-closed: **452,382** selected
units are quarantined/unrepresented, with **0** candidate and **0** eligible
units. The read-only census reports `static_authority_unavailable` and
`witness_authority_unavailable`. `cal:admission:genesis` reports the same
absence through deterministic blockers, and
`authority:overlap:verify --root /Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3
--tool-profile admission-static-ledgers-v1` exits 2 with
`overlap_current_missing`. The admission tree has no static/overlap current or
generation, source-generation authority, witness authority, or
`review/admission/sources` tree. Passing the draft `source-register.json`
instead of the genesis register is invalid and must remain rejected. The
bounded Mendeley and OSS-forge inputs remain quarantine-only; no third source
is authorized before the evidence, census, rights, lineage, family, pair,
privacy, and quality gates close.

The explicit package-local self-scan was reviewed as runtime and UX evidence:
**235/235** files analyzed, zero parse/timeout/crash/internal failures,
**157** active findings (147 low `ai/compression-profile`, 6 medium
`logic/zipf-slope-anomaly`, 4 medium `logic/heaps-deviation`), security
100/100 with zero security findings, hygiene 99.5168, and repository health
92.9403. AI Slop Score is **17.2869** (displayed as 17.3), above the configured
meanSlop policy of 15. The old baseline is rejected for a config-hash mismatch
and no replacement baseline is accepted. This is a policy failure, not a
runtime failure. The compression signal is broad across ordinary TypeScript
and cannot be treated as authorship evidence without authoritative v10.3
precision/FPR replay; do not refactor production code merely to lower this
score. The next calibration slice must measure per-source/group precision and
FPR, include repetitive-TypeScript controls, decide whether a second signal is
needed, and preserve the distinction between diagnostic output and release
evidence. The brief report should also distinguish policy failure from scanner
failure, show the active-rule breakdown, and document that `--no-telemetry`
does not disable project-memory writes when that setting is enabled.

The CLI audit confirms that the current executable exposes only the existing
evidence, acquisition, register, tool-authority, overlap, and recovery
commands. It does **not** parse or dispatch the planned
`rebuild:pre-witness`, `static-authority:recover`, or `census:preview` commands,
and it lacks the documented input-generation proposal, expected-current-static
generation, absent-current, and real-scale receipt flags. The adapter is a
library-only fixture boundary and currently hard-codes the nested
`admission-static-ledgers-v1` / `authority:overlap` selector; that receipt must
not be mislabeled as the outer `rebuild:pre-witness` authority. The next code
slice therefore needs an explicit outer rebuild transaction/receipt and a
fully materialized graph (including candidate semantic-authority bytes) before
it can mutate anything. Parser-only wiring or an empty/placeholder ledger is
not an implementation of the plan. Until that boundary exists and is
independently reviewed, real-corpus replay, label promotion, extra repository
pulls, manifest generation, release, publish, and deploy remain blocked by
evidence rather than by lack of disk space or worker capacity.

This audit supersedes older diagnostic counts in the handoff; it does not
advance any admission checkbox. The ordered next steps are: (1) independently
review the adapter and implement the explicit mutating CLI boundary with
fixture-scale tests; (2) harden staging/atomic-snapshot semantics and recovery;
(3) replay the real static/witness context only after byte-backed authority
exists; (4) calibrate self-scan policy and report UX against authoritative
labels; and (5) proceed to witnesses, census, smoke, canary, and release gates
only from eligible records. Do not pull more repositories or promote labels
while the two authority blockers remain.

## Task 2B bounded verification update — 2026-07-15

Verification is now risk-scaled for the current boundary rather than repeated
recursively after every test-only edit. The parser-visible
`rebuild:pre-witness` and `static-authority:recover` commands are strict and
fail closed with structured `authority_cli_unavailable` output before any
filesystem access; they do not pretend that the fixture overlap adapter is the
outer real-corpus rebuild. Their CLI boundary tests pass **10/10**. The brief
renderer contract tests pass **12/12**, and SlopBrick typecheck passes.

The watch-mode failure seen only under the full package load was diagnosed as a
test synchronization race: health is persisted before the report file is
rendered, and the test treated health as a render-complete marker. The test now
waits for the expected complete output content; the complete watch matrix passes
**45/45** serially. This is a test-boundary correction, not evidence that the
real-corpus admission gate is open. Production report writes still use ordinary
file replacement; atomic temp-file publication is a separate hardening item and
is not being folded into this admission slice.

The previously attempted full package run had **316/321** test files passing
with the watch race as the only failure after the stale-build-map issue was
corrected. A stable full recursive gate remains a commit/release checkpoint,
not a prerequisite for every local documentation or test synchronization edit.
The authority blockers, zero eligible units, no-pull rule, and no-release rule
are unchanged.

## Task 2B candidate context, census preview, and report publication update — 2026-07-15

The next bounded slice is now implemented and independently exercised at the
fixture boundary. Runtime context accepts a source generation marked
`independent_review` only when its exact canonical source proposal, approval,
blind assignment, two decisions, blind-review receipt, and generation-local
`source-semantic-authority.json` are present, self-hashed, graph-valid, and
contained. Genesis-quarantine sources remain sidecar-free. Candidate semantic
authority bytes are included in the aggregate source-authority proof, so the
context cannot silently ignore a candidate's provenance sidecar. The focused
positive and tamper/missing-sidecar tests pass **2/2** (the wider context
hardening file remains green).

`census:preview` is now a strict, non-persisting command. It requires the
verified admission-context profile, invocation selector, and exact source
register/reviews selectors, emits deterministic canonical JSON to stdout, and
reports the current census without creating authority. A 329-source fixture
proves canonical output, missing-selector rejection, unknown-option rejection,
and a byte-identical root snapshot (**3/3**). This does not make the real
corpus ready: the live replay remains **0 candidate / 0 eligible** with
`static_authority_unavailable` and `witness_authority_unavailable`.

The report writer now publishes JSON/HTML/heatmap files through a unique
temporary sibling followed by one rename, and watch filtering ignores those
scanner-owned temporary events. The brief report explicitly distinguishes a
runtime/incomplete scan from a policy-threshold failure and shows a bounded
active-rule summary. The same live `census:preview` command was run against
`/Users/cheng/corpus-expansion/v10.3` with the indexed context intent; it
returned canonical JSON without mutation, `ready=false`, 329/329
registered/reviewed sources, 452,382 additive unrepresented units, and blockers
`static_authority_unavailable` and `witness_authority_unavailable` (113,470
bytes; output SHA-256
`95ed5b57a4ccab0bd3eb21aef150088a34632b60f843f0200c204dc65e50ffda`). The
full pretty headline also shows an explicit
`[POLICY PASS]` or `[POLICY FAIL]` marker beside the absolute slop band, so a
green `LOW` band cannot be mistaken for a passing configured gate. The focused
renderer UX/contract pair passes **71/71** (the broader renderer/heatmap slice
remains **25/25**), the complete
watch-mode matrix passes **45/45** serially, SlopBrick typecheck and build
pass (the existing Zod declaration warnings are non-fatal), and
`git diff --check` is clean. The stable recursive workspace gate also passes:
Core **226/226**, engine **59/59**, website **38/38**, and SlopBrick
**318 passed / 5 skipped test files; 3,635 passed / 9 skipped tests**, with
recursive typecheck and build green. The known Zod declaration warnings and
fixture-only stderr remain non-fatal build/test diagnostics.

The outer mutating `rebuild:pre-witness` and
`static-authority:recover` orchestration is still deliberately unavailable:
the parser rejects option leakage and nested actions, then returns structured
`authority_cli_unavailable` before filesystem access. The fixture-scale
library adapter and nested overlap receipt are not a real-corpus rebuild.
Therefore no authority publication, corpus pull, label promotion, manifest,
release, publish, or deploy is authorized. The next implementation slice is
the fully materialized outer transaction/receipt and recovery path; after that
and its independent review, replay the existing corpus before considering any
additional sources.

## Task 2B transaction-owned staging hardening checkpoint — 2026-07-15

The independent adapter review approves the candidate-aware rebuild adapter
only as a fixture-scale library boundary. It identified a concrete
publication/recovery gap: proposal, source-proposal/approval, and
input-generation bytes were written directly to final paths before later
transaction stages. The publisher now stages those bytes under the
transaction-owned `review/admission/authority/staging-aux/<transactionId>`
subtree, verifies exact bytes, promotes with no-clobber renames, accepts an
identical already-promoted final on recovery replay, and removes only that
transaction's auxiliary staging after complete or explicit lock-only cleanup.
Input-generation artifacts are promoted as a verified directory. The static
generation staging directory remains separate so auxiliary files can never be
accidentally promoted into an immutable static generation; unknown files inside
promoted source/static generations remain preserved.

The focused publication/recovery suite is **15/15** and the adapter plus
loader suites are **17/17**; SlopBrick typecheck and `git diff --check` pass.
This closes the identified staging gap but not Task 2B: the outer mutating CLI
remains unavailable because there is still no real graph materializer, nested
publication-handoff integration, privacy/quality/lineage builder, real-scale
resource receipt, or witness authority. The live v10.3 replay remains
**329/329** reviewed sources, **452,382** quarantined/unrepresented units,
zero candidate/eligible, with blockers
`static_authority_unavailable` and `witness_authority_unavailable`. No corpus
bytes, labels, repository pulls, manifest, release, publish, or deployment
state changed.

## Task 2B nested publication handoff contract helper — 2026-07-15

Core now exposes a pure builder for the existing
`v10.3-nested-publication-handoff-v1` contract. The builder derives a child
recovery nonce from the parent transaction and nonce, expected current state,
child slot, and the exact infrastructure or profiled child selector. It then
computes the handoff self-hash and validates the strict branch shape, so
infrastructure-only fields cannot leak into profiled handoffs (or vice versa).
The helper performs no filesystem access or publication and does not imply
that the outer authority materializer exists.

The bounded Core gate is green: **31 test files / 231 tests**, typecheck,
codegen-freshness/contract verification, and build. Five focused tests cover
both child branches, completed state, invalid nonce input, and post-build
tampering. No schema version bump was needed because the wire schema is
unchanged.

This does not close Task 2B. Slot-set/order validation, parent/child lock and
transaction binding, the real byte-backed outer graph materializer, nested
handoff persistence/recovery, privacy/quality/lineage builders, real-scale
resource receipt, and witness authority remain open. The live corpus remains
**329/329** reviewed sources with **452,382** quarantined/unrepresented units,
zero candidate/eligible units, and blockers
`static_authority_unavailable` and `witness_authority_unavailable`. No corpus
bytes, labels, repository pulls, manifest, release, publish, or deployment
state changed. The outer mutating CLI therefore remains fail-closed.

## Task 2B explicit artifact preflight and CAS boundary audit — 2026-07-15

The next safe boundary is now available as a read-only helper,
`preflightAdmissionArtifacts`. It accepts a complete caller-supplied list of
project-root-relative `review/admission/...` files and reports deterministic
per-item `present`, `missing`, or `invalid` status plus structured
`request_invalid`, `root_unavailable`, `missing_input`, and `invalid_input`
errors. It checks regular-file type, containment, symlink-free ancestors,
exact optional byte lengths, and optional SHA-256 commitments. It performs no
directory discovery, repair, authority inference, or writes; a `ready` result
is only an input-presence result, not a graph or policy pass. Focused coverage
is **4/4**, and SlopBrick typecheck passes.

The CAS audit also closes an ambiguity in the fixture publisher. Core and the
read-only loader correctly accept and rehash source-generation
`admission_root_content_addressed` bundle receipts at the fixed
`evidence-cas/sha256/<prefix>/<sha256>` path, but the fixture publisher has no
CAS reservation/reuse transaction. It now documents and tests a fail-closed
rejection before lock creation rather than copying a CAS object into a
generation-local directory. The publication suite is **16/16**; no CAS bytes
are promoted or removed. The generic preflight is intentionally not wired to
publication until role-specific Core receipt validation and CAS transaction
ownership exist.

The outer mutating CLI remains unavailable, and the live v10.3 corpus remains
**329/329** reviewed, **452,382** quarantined/unrepresented, zero
candidate/eligible, with `static_authority_unavailable` and
`witness_authority_unavailable`. No corpus bytes, labels, repository pulls,
manifest, release, publish, or deployment state changed.

## Current corpus allocation/provenance checkpoint — 2026-07-15

The 452,382-unit corpus does **not** require a person to open and judge every
file. The first pass is deterministic accounting: establish where each unit
came from, assign one material owner, and make every unresolved unit explicit.
The current control plane already proves the source-level conservation
`58,089 baseline + 394,293 repository = 452,382 selected` across **329** source
IDs (**317** repository material leaves, one baseline material source, ten
non-selected material sources, and one non-additive aggregate inventory view).
The raw discovery population, **1,478,350**, stays a separate denominator.

That is not yet row-level provenance. The `legacy-v5-inventory` aggregate
reports 394,293 candidate units from an open-world inventory and is not itself
an additive owner. The 317 source reviews are all truthful
`source_quarantine`; every review has `review_incomplete` and
`source_wide_quarantine`, and the current review evidence is not closed-world
or sufficient to prove AI authorship. Repository origin/commit observations and
declared AI/human polarity are useful intake evidence, but a declaration is not
an eligible `verified_ai`/`verified_human` label.

The next safe slice is therefore a read-only, deterministic allocation ledger
before any new repository pull or manual labeling campaign. It will join the
existing register, source reviews, pinned repository/materialization receipts,
inventory row hashes, origin/commit/tree/path identities, rights evidence, and
duplicate/overlap results. Each selected unit will receive exactly one
`sourceId`/material owner or an explicit `unrepresented`/`quarantine`
disposition with reason codes; aggregate inventory rows remain non-additive.
The ledger must prove `452,382 = 58,089 + 394,293`, keep 1,478,350 raw units
outside that denominator, and never infer a label from a folder, repository
name, or inventory count. It can be streamed and sharded under the existing
static-ledger resource limits, so it does not require loading the corpus into
memory.

Only after this allocation ledger is complete do we spend review effort on a
bounded, independently assigned sample of candidate rows (smoke **100 AI +
100 human**, then canary **5,000 + 5,000** from `eligible_gold`). Manual or
independent adjudication remains necessary for authorship, rights/lineage,
family/pair leakage, privacy, and quality; allocation answers “where did this
unit come from?” and does not by itself answer “is this an authoritative AI or
human label?”. No admission checkbox, candidate count, eligibility count,
manifest, release, or deployment advances until the ledger and its authority
inputs are independently reviewed.

## Allocation preview implementation checkpoint — 2026-07-15

The bounded allocation/provenance preview is implemented at commit
`d1bf476d3`. It consumes the two explicit v10.3 inventory streams without
loading them into memory, validates the 329-entry Core register/review set
before consumption, canonicalizes non-canonical JSONL input, and emits one
diagnostic ownership row per inventory record. The preview proves exact
conservation: **452,382** rows emitted (**224,903 positive / 227,479
negative**), split into **58,089 baseline / 394,293 repository** rows, with
**0** duplicates and **0** unrepresented rows. Every current row remains
`quarantine`; no row is promoted to a verified label. The real-stream replay
is deterministic with stream SHA-256
`7dfec0cebf6a169cbfa10ba8955f038cb5b6dc74010245a52e1a5cd9b8669097` and
register SHA-256 `ce40134968cd9f490b29e695b27fb724ce8d4b8ba9a4abf26eb789cc4c4d78de`.

The focused suite is **21/21** serially, SlopBrick typecheck passes, and the
working-tree diff is clean for this code slice. The preview is explicitly
`ready=false`, `authorityEligible=false`, and `diagnosticOnly=true`; it does
not publish a ledger, alter corpus bytes, or satisfy static/witness authority.
The remaining blocker is the real outer graph materializer and authority
transaction, not exhaustive manual inspection of all rows.

## Outer authority CLI boundary checkpoint — 2026-07-15

The outer command boundary is now executable for an explicitly supplied,
byte-backed graph in commits `38258d703`, `3a427e9aa`, `c89f40bdd`, and
`2fbde2bf2`.
`rebuild:pre-witness` and `static-authority:recover` require caller-selected
proposal, input-generation, and candidate-current paths, indexed tool-receipt
selectors, and strict source proposal/semantic-authority bytes. They invoke the
existing loader and transaction-owned adapter; they do not discover a graph or
construct privacy/quality/lineage ledgers. Create publication and pending
transaction recovery, including a valid lock-only cleanup, are covered by the fixture CLI suite, and the combined
CLI/overlap/loader/adapter/publication review gate is **5 files / 50/50** focused
tests with
SlopBrick typecheck and diff-check green.

The output deliberately includes `authorityScope=prebuilt-diagnostic`,
`realScaleReceiptVerified=false`, `ready=false`, `authorityEligible=false`,
and `diagnosticOnly=true`. The required `--require-real-scale-receipt` flag is
currently only an explicit indexed-receipt selector acknowledgement; it does
not prove real-scale coverage, resource limits, static authority, witness
authority, or corpus readiness. The outer commands require the project root
(the parent of `review/admission`); they reject a nested admission root rather
than silently changing path meaning. The live v10.3 root still lacks the
explicit graph and remains quarantine-only; no corpus bytes, labels, pulls,
manifest, release, publish, or deployment state changed.

The review deliberately stops at the risk-scaled boundary: exact streamed
conservation and byte/hash ownership cover the full corpus, while bounded
fixture and sentinel checks cover recovery and UX. It does not require a
manual read of all 452,382 rows. Minor follow-ups are recorded rather than
blocking admission: clarify the scope of the lock-only `verificationSha256`
field and add a CLI assertion that pending stderr carries `recoveryNonce`.

## 22. Primary research and platform references

The first version of this roadmap was repository-audit based and had no external citations. The following sources now support the amended gates:

- [Codex `AGENTS.md` discovery](https://developers.openai.com/codex/guides/agents-md) — layered repository instruction discovery and configurable byte budget
- [Claude Code project memory](https://docs.anthropic.com/en/docs/claude-code/memory) — `CLAUDE.md`, scoped rules, `AGENTS.md` imports, auto memory, and context-size guidance
- [GitHub Copilot repository instructions](https://docs.github.com/en/copilot/customizing-copilot/adding-repository-custom-instructions-for-github-copilot) — nested `AGENTS.md` and root adapter support
- [GitHub Copilot Memory](https://docs.github.com/en/copilot/concepts/agents/copilot-memory) — cited repository facts, branch validation, repository scope, and retention behavior
- [Node.js release status](https://nodejs.org/en/about/previous-releases) — Node 20 is EOL; production should use maintained LTS lines
- [JSON Schema Draft 2020-12 validation](https://json-schema.org/draft/2020-12/json-schema-validation) — assertion and format-validation contract
- [Original Louvain paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/0803.0476) — modularity optimization basis
- [TypeScript module-resolution reference](https://www.typescriptlang.org/docs/handbook/modules/reference) — package exports/types behavior
- [scikit-learn GroupKFold](https://scikit-learn.org/stable/modules/generated/sklearn.model_selection.GroupKFold.html) — non-overlapping source groups
- [Kapoor and Narayanan on ML leakage](https://pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/articles/PMC10499856/) — leakage taxonomy and reproducibility risk

## Current correction — outer materializer authority boundary (2026-07-15)

The earlier CLI paragraph is historical and must not be read as a successful
publication path. Commits `3cf05569c` and `d25914f26` make the outer commands
require explicit bundle, overlap-generation/envelope, indexed-tool, and stream
selectors; missing or adapter-only invocations fail closed, and public output
keeps `realScaleReceiptVerified=false`. Commit `f62013fbc` adds the declared
overlap artifact byte map (including shards), rehashes every receipt, parses
both JSONL streams line-by-line, binds rows to the normalizer/summary, and
joins the privacy/quality/lineage ledgers to the admission stream IDs. The
caller-supplied expectation must equal the bound stream, so a one-record
fixture cannot be labeled as the 452,382-record corpus.

The bounded fixture gate is **27/27** focused tests (7 materializer, 8
resource-receipt, 6 static-ledger, 7 CLI), with SlopBrick typecheck and
`git diff --check` green. This is still diagnostic-only: the live v10.3 root
has no authoritative graph, overlap shard tree, witness evidence, or
full-scale resource receipt; no corpus bytes, labels, repository pulls,
manifest, release, publish, or deployment changed. The next gate is explicit
real-corpus authority materialization followed by the bounded 100+100 smoke
and 5,000+5,000 canary witness checks.

## Risk-scaled provenance allocation replay — 2026-07-15

The read-only allocation preview was replayed against the current v10.3
inventory using the Core-validated genesis register/review set and the two
explicit JSONL inventory streams. It consumed the streams once with bounded
memory; it did not retain the 452,382 rows or write corpus artifacts. The
replay validated **329/329** source reviews, exact polarity and ownership
bindings, zero duplicate IDs, zero unknown repositories, zero aggregate-owner
rows, zero path/SHA/commit/origin mismatches, and exact source-level count
conservation.

The canonical result is **452,382** rows (**224,903 declared AI / 227,479
declared human; 58,089 baseline / 394,293 repository**), with **0 allocated,
452,382 quarantined, 0 unrepresented, 0 duplicates, and no stream errors**.
The diagnostic stream SHA-256 is
`7dfec0cebf6a169cbfa10ba8955f038cb5b6dc74010245a52e1a5cd9b8669097`; the
register SHA-256 is
`ce40134968cd9f490b29e695b27fb724ce8d4b8ba9a4abf26eb789cc4c4d78de`. The
positive and negative inventory hashes are
`4511193d10cd39ac7589047e945c531d20752b3344b1d22e96a9d348bc7d34f0` and
`85ef9452e96977ec21578a8f87026d374ac510daad20fd34af8d6d363b38c215`.

This answers the corpus-review question: provenance and allocation can be
checked at source/stream level without manually reading every file. It does
not make the declared AI/human polarity an authoritative label. Every row
therefore remains quarantine because authorship, evidence, rights, source
bytes, static authority, and witness authority are not yet independently
materialized. No additional public-repository pull is justified by this
replay; first persist the missing canonical register/source generations and
receipts, then publish the allocation ledger and rerun the same byte-bound
checks.

The package self-scan accounting follow-up is now closed: persisted
`inventory.json` and `structure.md` report the same **240** files as the
health/report coverage, while the progress renderer emits `<1s` rather than a
misleading `0s` ETA for positive sub-second estimates. The AI score remains
the diagnostic **17.6 > 15** policy failure; this UX correction does not alter
calibration or release readiness. Evidence and implementation details are in
`.superpowers/sdd/task-allocation-report.md`.

### Scale-safety correction for the next authority slice

The allocation preview is genuinely streaming, but the current pure static
ledger builders accept arrays of verified records/results. They must not be
called with all 452,382 rows in one JavaScript object: that would defeat the
bounded-memory contract and reintroduce the RAM risk. The next real-authority
implementation must add a disk-backed JSONL ledger adapter (or equivalent
external-sort pipeline) that preserves canonical order, exact record-set
hashes, unresolved partitions, and receipt byte identity under one worker and
the documented heap cap before the outer materializer can consume live data.

## RAM-safe static-ledger stream checkpoint — 2026-07-15

The next authority slice is implemented at commit `ee4392f43`. The new
`admission-static-ledger-stream.ts` adapter consumes canonical, strictly
ordered record/result/unresolved JSONL streams with one worker and bounded
per-row memory. It validates Core record/result shapes and content hashes,
proves the partition, writes transaction-local JSONL projections, computes
record-set/stream/semantic ledger hashes by sequential file reads, and
publishes one no-clobber output directory. It is explicitly
`diagnosticOnly=true` and `authorityEligible=false`; it does not read the
v10.3 corpus, promote labels, or replace the outer authority materializer.

The focused adapter suite is **3/3**, the combined allocation/static-ledger
suite is **30/30**, SlopBrick typecheck and build pass, and `git diff --check`
passes. The existing non-fatal Zod declaration warnings remain unchanged.
Commit `de0830832` now binds optional stream receipts and their
generation-local projection paths into the explicit outer materializer. It
validates the receipt's record-set/semantic hash and partition against the
pre-witness bundle, rehashes every declared projection artifact, and fails
closed when a projection is missing or substituted. The materializer remains
diagnostic-only and still requires the full byte-backed graph; this is not
real-corpus authority. The next gate is one integrated fixture check, then a
real-scale attempt only after source evidence and rights/authorship inputs are
materialized.

## Integrated authority gate and live census replay — 2026-07-15

The consolidated fixture gate is **6 files / 52 tests**, serially, covering
the stream adapter, array-ledger contracts, outer materializer, CLI boundary,
rebuild adapter, and allocation preview. It passes with SlopBrick typecheck
and `git diff --check` green. The live read-only `census:preview` replay still
returns `ready=false`, `authorityEligible=false`, **329/329** registered and
reviewed sources, **452,382** additive unrepresented/quarantine units, and
zero candidate/eligible units; blockers remain
`static_authority_unavailable` and `witness_authority_unavailable`. Therefore
the 100+100 smoke and 5,000+5,000 canary are correctly deferred rather than
run against declared, unverified polarity.

### Verification consolidation — 2026-07-15

The earlier parallel review slices overlapped on contract and edge-case
confirmation. They are consolidated here: one owner implements the bounded
ledger slice, one integrated gate reviews its output, and the smoke/canary
checks are the only downstream calibration runs. Adversarial edge cases stay
as focused tests; they do not trigger another full-corpus replay. No manual
review of all 452,382 rows and no additional repository pull is planned unless
the authoritative allocation or eligible-gold counts show a real deficit.

## Final package-wide quality gate — 2026-07-15

After the integrated gate exposed two CLI message-order regressions and one
millisecond timing flake, the parser now reports the required graph selectors
without losing the stable `requires explicit graph paths` contract, rejects a
nested outer action before the completeness check, and the cache benchmark
guards against a zero-millisecond cold parse. The checked-in `dist` source maps
were rebuilt. The affected suites pass **20/20**; the final serial SlopBrick
package gate passes **325 test files / 3,697 tests**, with **5 skipped files / 9
skipped tests**. Package typecheck and build are green; build emits only the
existing non-fatal Zod declaration warnings. This is the one final quality gate

## 22. Primary research and platform references (continued)

- [Saito and Rehmsmeier on precision-recall evaluation](https://journals.plos.org/plosone/article?id=10.1371/journal.pone.0118432) — imbalanced-class evaluation
- [Benjamini and Hochberg](https://doi.org/10.1111/j.2517-6161.1995.tb02031.x) — multiple-testing false-discovery control
- [Droid: AI-generated code detection resources](https://aclanthology.org/2025.emnlp-main.1593/) — cross-model/domain/language, coauthored, and adversarial evaluation
- [Datasheets for Datasets](https://doi.org/10.1145/3458723) and [Model Cards](https://doi.org/10.1145/3287560.3287596) — data/model reporting
- [NIST AI RMF](https://www.nist.gov/publications/artificial-intelligence-risk-management-framework-ai-rmf-10) and [2026 monitoring report](https://www.nist.gov/news-events/news/2026/03/new-report-challenges-monitoring-deployed-ai-systems) — TEVV, limits, drift, and post-deployment monitoring
- [GitHub rulesets](https://docs.github.com/en/repositories/configuring-branches-and-merges-in-your-repository/managing-rulesets/available-rules-for-rulesets), [secure Actions use](https://docs.github.com/en/actions/reference/security/secure-use), and [deployment environments](https://docs.github.com/en/actions/concepts/workflows-and-actions/deployment-environments) — protected branches, immutable action references, and job gating
- [npm trusted publishing](https://docs.npmjs.com/trusted-publishers/) and [staged publishing](https://docs.npmjs.com/staged-publishing/) — OIDC provenance and review-before-publication
- [Cloudflare Pages Git integration](https://developers.cloudflare.com/pages/configuration/git-integration/) and [preview deployments](https://developers.cloudflare.com/pages/configuration/preview-deployments/) — deployment ownership and preview contracts
- [HumanVSAI_CodeDataset on Mendeley Data](https://data.mendeley.com/datasets/kjh95n54f8/1) and [its DataCite DOI record](https://api.datacite.org/dois/10.17632/kjh95n54f8.1) — the pinned v1 archive, dataset-level CC BY 4.0, and version discrepancy recorded by the quarantine audit
- [OSS-forge HumanVsAICode](https://huggingface.co/datasets/OSS-forge/HumanVsAICode) and [the ISSRE paper](https://doi.org/10.1109/ISSRE66568.2025.00035) — paired human/model fields and source-wide generation claims, not row-level authority
- [HMCorp paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2411.04704) and [CodeSearchNet](https://github.com/github/CodeSearchNet) — upstream reconstruction and per-language source-license evidence required before promotion

root mutation. A routing-promotion crash test specifically proves recovery
reuses the lock's original compare-and-swap state rather than rebinding to a

## Smoke materializer integrity hardening — 2026-07-16

The smoke adapter now tracks staging-directory ownership. If a replay or
concurrent invocation encounters an existing `.staging-*` directory, it fails
closed without deleting the other transaction's bytes; cleanup is limited to a
directory created by the current invocation. A regression test preserves a
foreign staging sentinel. The cohort validator also now requires every
declared source to be represented by at least one record, rather than counting
only the supplied source sidecars. Focused coverage is **4/4**, SlopBrick
typecheck and rebuild pass, and `git diff --check` is clean. This remains a

## Smoke source-approval byte binding — 2026-07-16

Each smoke source now requires a canonical independent-review approval object
and exact bytes. The approval ID/hash and proposal ID/hash must match the

typecheck, rebuild, and diff checks green. This strengthens the input boundary
only; it does not establish semantic source authority or change the corpus.

## Explicit smoke-input CLI boundary — 2026-07-16

The library-only smoke materializer now has a deliberately thin CLI adapter,
`admission:smoke-input`. It accepts exactly one caller-supplied, canonical,
root-relative manifest (`--manifest`) plus an explicit root. The manifest
names the two source-generation/proposal/approval/review/semantic-authority
sidecars, register delta, canonical admission-record JSONL, overlap universe,
normalizer registry, overlap-universe JSONL, and an existing output directory.
Every named file is resolved through the contained/symlink-aware path guard;
the CLI performs no corpus discovery, repository pull, label inference, or
authority promotion. The materializer remains the sole writer and emits only
`diagnosticOnly=true` / `authorityEligible=false` output.

The CLI boundary has four focused fail-closed tests: missing manifest,
root-escape manifest, incomplete manifest before materialization, and
`--manifest` rejection on unrelated admission commands. The implementation
is ready for an owner-supplied pinned authority bundle, but no real bundle was
loaded in this slice and no corpus, label, authority, release, remote, or
deployment state changed. The live census therefore remains **0 represented /
0 eligible**, blocked by `static_authority_unavailable` and
`witness_authority_unavailable`.

## Complete source-generation graph validation — 2026-07-16

The smoke materializer now routes each complete semantic sidecar through Core's
`validateCalibrationAdmissionSourceGenerationGraphV1` validator. Source review,
proposal, generation, approval, blind assignment, both typed decisions, blind
review receipt, and the acquired materialization snapshot/receipt must agree;
ID-only or partial sidecars fail closed before staging. The focused materializer
coverage is **10/10** and the CLI-plus-materializer gate is **14/14**. The test
fixture uses a fully typed acquired graph; no evidence is fabricated and the
result remains diagnostic-only. The external authority bundle is still required
before a real smoke run, so the census remains **0 represented / 0 eligible**
with `static_authority_unavailable` and `witness_authority_unavailable`.

## Static-ledger stream hostile-runtime and receipt hardening — 2026-07-16

The disk-backed static-ledger stream now fails closed for hostile JavaScript
requests before dereferencing request fields, returning a typed diagnostic
receipt for null and invalid-kind inputs. Successful stream receipts now require
an explicit empty error list, an absolute output directory, and exact
generation-local projection paths for the selected ledger kind; traversal,
absolute, and cross-kind paths are rejected. The focused stream plus outer
materializer gate is **14/14**, with SlopBrick typecheck, build, and
`git diff --check` green (only the existing non-fatal Zod declaration warnings).
This is local safety hardening only: no corpus, label, authority, release,
remote, or deployment state changed, and the live census remains **0
represented / 0 eligible** with the two authority blockers above.

## Smoke-input boundary hardening and exploratory-role clarification — 2026-07-16

The explicit `admission:smoke-input` loader now accepts only canonical
root-relative manifest selectors and manifest paths: dot/dot-dot or empty
segments, repeated separators, backslashes, control bytes, and overlong paths
fail before input resolution. The contained loader also rejects directories and
other non-regular files before reading bytes, preventing a caller-supplied FIFO
or device path from blocking the diagnostic command. The materializer rejects
admission JSONL that is not strictly ordered by immutable `recordId`, matching
the downstream static-authority stream contract. Focused CLI/materializer
coverage is **19/19** serial, SlopBrick typecheck is green, and `git diff
--check` is clean.

This adapter remains intentionally exploratory and diagnostic-only: it enforces
the explicit 100/100 record shape, source/language/family/pair mechanics, byte
bindings, and overlap joins, but it does not infer `eligible_gold` or claim a
verified `AdmissionCohortWitnessV1`. Gold evidence, unique-cluster authority,
complete static ledgers, witness approval, and release readiness remain
downstream gates; every materialized result is `diagnosticOnly=true`,
`authorityEligible=false`, and `ready=false`. No corpus, labels, authority,
remote, release, or deployment state changed.

## Static-ledger receipt invariant hardening — 2026-07-16

Static-ledger receipt validation now binds the selected kind's exact ledger
version and the one-worker execution contract. The public stream boundary also
survives a hostile JavaScript request whose property getter throws, returning a
typed diagnostic failure instead of throwing from its fallback path. Focused
static-ledger coverage is **7/7** serial and SlopBrick typecheck passes. This is
local fail-closed hardening only; no corpus, labels, authority, release,
remote, or deployment state changed.

## Lock-only verification-scope clarification — 2026-07-16

`verificationSha256` on the prebuilt outer-adapter result is a raw-byte proof
of the graph reopened and validated by that adapter. It is not a publication
receipt, real-scale resource receipt, static-authority result, witness result,
or readiness claim. A lock-only cleanup may return the same graph proof while
setting `durableGraphVerified=false`; callers must use that flag and the
publication `status` to distinguish durable publication from lock cleanup.
The pending-stderr recovery-nonce assertion remains a separate, non-blocking
CLI follow-up.

## Admission reader `O_NOFOLLOW` capability guard — 2026-07-16

The two pathname-bound authority readers now share an explicit capability
contract. They require a positive `O_NOFOLLOW` primitive and reject Windows
reparse-point semantics; there is no plain-path fallback. Unsupported hosts
fail closed with a platform-specific diagnostic before authority bytes are
read. This makes the supported POSIX policy explicit while preserving the
existing containment walk, regular-file check, and final realpath comparison.

The focused security, artifact-preflight, and authority-loader suite passes
**20/20**, and SlopBrick typecheck plus package build pass. This closes the
capability/fallback P2 only. A descriptor-relative root/snapshot (or equivalent)
is still a separate open hardening for the residual check-then-open TOCTOU
window; no corpus, authority, release, publish, or deployment state changed.

## Admission reader file-identity binding — 2026-07-16

The loader and explicit artifact preflight now bind each pathname read to the
device/inode observed before open, the identity reported by the opened
descriptor, and the identity observed after the read. A replacement by another
regular file therefore fails closed even when the replacement is not a symlink;
the existing canonical-path and `O_NOFOLLOW` checks remain in force.

The focused security, artifact-preflight, and authority-loader suite passes
**21/21**, SlopBrick typecheck passes, and the package build passes. This is the
portable identity-check equivalent that narrows the file-replacement portion
of the TOCTOU window. A true immutable descriptor-relative directory snapshot
is still not claimed because Node exposes no portable `openat`-style primitive;
no corpus, authority, release, publish, or deployment state changed.

## Clean recursive workspace gate replay — 2026-07-16

A disposable detached checkout of commit
`f067c484ec09996c17a26c3a2a5a5fd6224a6d0c` was verified with the same
RAM-capped, one-worker policy and with generated outputs excluded from the
clean-status identity. A cold-checkout `pnpm -r typecheck` attempted before
build exposed an ordering caveat: the Engine example programs import
`@usebrick/engine/pure`, whose generated `dist/pure` entry does not exist until
the package has been built. This is not a source failure; the supported clean
gate order is **build → typecheck → test**. After the build, recursive
typecheck passed for all four packages.

The clean recursive build passed with only the existing non-fatal Zod
declaration warnings. The subsequent serial recursive test gate passed all
four workspace packages: Core **33 files / 240 tests**, Website **11 files /
47 tests**, Engine **5 files / 59 tests**, and SlopBrick **333 files / 3,748
tests**, with SlopBrick's expected **5 skipped files / 9 skipped tests**. The
expected stderr fixtures, `fatal: not a git repository` messages from isolated
test fixtures, and `shellcheck not installed; skipping` notice were non-failing
test output. The detached checkout returned an empty clean-status result after
the gate and was removed without touching the active checkout.

This closes the clean local recursive verification prerequisite. The packed
artifact receipt immediately before this documentation commit remains bound
to commit `7fa55a6e7ba6e6e950559db3570a3015bf77bc03`; any release candidate
must rebuild and rebind its artifact, checksums, and consumer receipts to the
final approved package commit after documentation and code changes stop. No
corpus bytes, labels, authority, calibration, release, remote, publish, or
deployment state changed.

The evidence is useful but still non-authoritative. HumanEval has **100 AI / 100
human** paired records with **92 content-distinct** pairs and **8 permanently
content-unsafe** pair groups; its source contract still yields **0 eligible
pairs** because the generated AI arm is local/untracked and its generation
JSONL lacks an immutable HTTPS evidence reference. EvalPlus remains
`quarantine_diagnostic_only` with **164 globally quarantined pairs**, **11
content-unsafe** groups, and unresolved authorship, scaffold, release-asset,
generator-revision, licensing, and bytecode-disclosure blockers. The GPT-5
coding-examples audit likewise remains `source_quarantine` with source-register
delta, two-independent-decision, and derived-asset-policy blockers.

This refresh confirms that more repository acquisition is not justified by
current evidence. The next action is owner direction plus immutable source or
release-asset evidence for a bounded remediation; no labels, register entries,
static-ledger bytes, witness bytes, manifest, selection, run, release, or
external state changed.

## Cold-checkout Engine typecheck boundary fix — 2026-07-16

The clean recursive replay exposed one genuine quality-gate ordering defect:
before generated output existed, the Engine example programs could not resolve
their own public `@usebrick/engine/pure` export. A red proof in a detached
checkout failed with three `TS2307` errors for that subpath. The examples-only
`tsconfig.examples.json` now maps the package self-imports to `src/index.ts`
and `src/pure.ts`, without changing the published export map or runtime code.

The same detached checkout, still without Engine `dist/`, now passes recursive
workspace typecheck for Core, Website, Engine, and SlopBrick; the Engine test
package remains **5 files / 59 tests** green. This removes the cold-checkout
typecheck caveat. Build → typecheck → test remains the release verification
order because generated artifacts are still required by package tests and
packing. No corpus, authority, calibration, release, publish, or deployment
state changed.

## Cross-language unsupported-normalizer hardening — 2026-07-16

The optional Task 2A hardening is implemented at commit
`a7d3e0c18`. Core's overlap-universe validator, the incremental JSONL stream,
the bounded overlap builder, and the outer authority materializer now reject an
`unsupported` row whenever its normalizer ID appears anywhere in the frozen
registry, even when the row claims a different or unknown language. This closes
the registry-alias gap without changing the schema, labels, corpus bytes, or
authority state.

TDD evidence is red-to-green: the new Core and stream cases failed before the
fix because the invalid rows were accepted; after the fix Core overlap tests
pass **7/7**, stream tests **5/5**, the overlap builder/materializer/universe
focus passes **22/22**, Core codegen/schema validation passes, and Core and
SlopBrick typechecks pass. The current Core package regression is **33 test
files / 241 tests**; the earlier clean recursive gate's **240-test** count is
historical to its pre-hardening commit. The commit hook self-scan is diagnostic only (four
low compression-profile findings in the changed source files); it does not
alter release or calibration status. The previously bound clean artifact is no
longer the final package receipt; rebuild and rebind after the code boundary is
frozen.
